             & = 6\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{1}{\cos2x}}                                                                            \\
             & = 6
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Exercise 25.7a}

Find the limit of the following:
\begin{enumerate}
    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{x\cos x}{\sin2x}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{x\cos x}{\sin2x}} & = \dfrac{1}{2}\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(\dfrac{2x}{\sin2x}\cdot \cos x\right)} \\
                                                         & = \dfrac{1}{2}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
        \columnbreak{}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to0}(x\cot x)$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to0}(x\cot x) & = \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{x\cdot \cos x}{\sin x}}               \\
                                         & = \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(\dfrac{x}{\sin x} \cdot \cos x\right)} \\
                                         & = 1
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
    \end{multicols}

    \newpage
    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{2x}{\sin7x}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{2x}{\sin7x}} & = 2\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{x}{\sin7x}}             \\
                                                    & = \dfrac{2}{7}\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{7x}{\sin7x}} \\
                                                    & = \dfrac{2}{7}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
        \columnbreak{}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{\sin{\dfrac{5}{2}}x}{2x}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{\sin{\dfrac{5}{2}}x}{2x}} & = \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{\sin{\dfrac{5}{2}}x}{\dfrac{4}{5}\cdot\dfrac{5}{2}x}} \\
                                                                 & = \dfrac{5}{4}\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{\sin{\dfrac{5}{2}}x}{\dfrac{5}{2}x}}      \\
                                                                 & = \dfrac{5}{4}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
    \end{multicols}
    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{\sin(2x^{2})}{x}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{\sin(2x^{2})}{x}} & = 2\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{x^2\sin(2x^{2})}{2x^2}} \\
                                                         & = 2\lim\limits_{x\to0}{x^2}                           \\
                                                         & = 0
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
        \columnbreak{}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{x^{2}}{\sin^{2}b x}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{x^{2}}{\sin^{2}b x}} & = \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(\dfrac{x}{\sin bx}\right)^2}                \\
                                                            & = \dfrac{1}{b^2}\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(\dfrac{bx}{\sin bx}\right)^2} \\
                                                            & = \dfrac{1}{b^2}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
    \end{multicols}

    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{\sin^{2}3x}{2x^{2}}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{\sin^{2}3x}{2x^{2}}} & = \dfrac{1}{2}\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{\sin^{2}3x}{x^{2}}}         \\
                                                            & = \dfrac{1}{2}\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(\dfrac{\sin3x}{x}\right)^2}  \\
                                                            & = \dfrac{9}{2}\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(\dfrac{\sin3x}{3x}\right)^2} \\
                                                            & = \dfrac{9}{2}
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{4x}{\tan8x}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{4x}{\tan8x}} & = 4\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{x\cos8x}{\sin8x}}                                 \\
                                                    & = \dfrac{1}{2}\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(\dfrac{8x}{\sin8x} \cdot \cos8x\right)} \\
                                                    & = \dfrac{1}{2}
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}
    \newpage
    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{\sin5x}{\tan3x}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{\sin5x}{\tan3x}} & = \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(\dfrac{\sin5x}{\sin3x} \cdot \cos3x\right)}                            & \\
                                                        & = \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(\dfrac{\sin5x}{5x} \cdot \dfrac{3x}{\sin3x} \cdot \dfrac{5}{3}\right)}   \\
                                                        & = \dfrac{5}{3}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
        \columnbreak{}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{1-\cos4x}{x\sin5x}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{1-\cos4x}{x\sin5x}} & = \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{2\sin^{2}2x}{x\sin5x}}                                                                   & \\
                                                           & = 2\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(\dfrac{\sin^2 2x}{4x^2} \cdot \dfrac{5x}{\sin5x} \cdot \dfrac{4x}{5x}\right)}              \\
                                                           & = 2\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left[\left(\dfrac{\sin 2x}{2x}\right)^2 \cdot \dfrac{5x}{\sin5x} \cdot \dfrac{4x}{5x}\right]}   \\
                                                           & = 2 \cdot \dfrac{4}{5}                                                                                                  \\
                                                           & = \dfrac{8}{5}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
    \end{multicols}

    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{5x^{2}}{2\tan^{2}2x}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{5x^{2}}{2\tan^{2}2x}} & = \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{5x^{2}\cos^2 2x}{2\sin^{2}2x}}                       & \\
                                                             & = \dfrac{5}{2}\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(\dfrac{x\cos2x}{\sin2x}\right)^2}           \\
                                                             & = \dfrac{5}{8}\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(\dfrac{2x}{\sin2x} \cdot \cos2x\right)^2}   \\
                                                             & = \dfrac{5}{8}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
        \columnbreak{}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{\cos3x-1}{3x^{2}}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{\cos3x-1}{3x^{2}}} & = \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{1 - 2\sin^2 \dfrac{3x}{2} - 1}{3x^{2}}}                                            \\
                                                          & = -\dfrac{2}{3}\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\dfrac{\sin^2 \dfrac{3x}{2}}{x^{2}}}                                         \\
                                                          & = -\dfrac{2}{3}\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(\dfrac{\sin \dfrac{3x}{2}}{x}\right)^2}                                \\
                                                          & = -\dfrac{2}{3} \cdot \dfrac{9}{4}\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(\dfrac{\sin \dfrac{3x}{2}}{\dfrac{3x}{2}}\right)^2} \\
                                                          & = -\dfrac{3}{2}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
    \end{multicols}
\end{enumerate}

\newpage
\subsection*{B. $\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{{\left(1 + \dfrac{1}{x}\right)}^{x}}$}

Consider the limit of ${\left(1 + \dfrac{1}{x}\right)}^{x}$ as $x$ approaches
infinity. As $x \to \infty$, the changes of the function $f (x) = {\left(1 +
    \dfrac{1}{x}\right)}^{x}$ is shown in the table below:
\begin{center}
    \begin{NiceTabular}{|c|c|}[hvlines,cell-space-limits=5pt]
        $x$      & $f (x) = {\left(1 + \dfrac{1}{x}\right)}^{x}$             \\
        1        & ${\left(1 + \dfrac{1}{1}\right)}^{1} = 2$                 \\
        10       & ${\left(1 + \dfrac{1}{10}\right)}^{10} = 2.59374$         \\
        100      & ${\left(1 + \dfrac{1}{100}\right)}^{100} = 2.70481$       \\
        1000     & ${\left(1 + \dfrac{1}{1000}\right)}^{1000} = 2.71692$     \\
        10000    & ${\left(1 + \dfrac{1}{10000}\right)}^{10000} = 2.71815$   \\
        100000   & ${\left(1 + \dfrac{1}{100000}\right)}^{100000} = 2.71827$ \\
        $\vdots$ & $\vdots$                                                  \\
    \end{NiceTabular}
\end{center}

By looking at the table above, we can see that as $x$ approaches infinity, the
value of ${\left(1 + \dfrac{1}{x}\right)}^{x}$ approaches a constant value that
is denoted as $e$. $e$ is an irrational number and is approximately equal to
$2.71828182846$. It is called the \textbf{natural base}, and is one of the most
important numbers in mathematics and appears in many applications.

\begin{mdframed}[style=MyFrame]
    \begin{cequation}
        \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{{\left(1 + \dfrac{1}{x}\right)}^{x}} = e
    \end{cequation}
\end{mdframed}

If $y = \dfrac{1}{x}$, then $x = \dfrac{1}{y}$. As $x \to \infty$, $y \to 0$.

Therefore, $\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{{\left(1 + \dfrac{1}{x}\right)}^{x}} =
    \lim\limits_{y\to0}{{\left(1 + y\right)}^{\frac{1}{y}}} = e$.

\newpage
\subsection{Practice 9}

Find the limit of the following:
\begin{enumerate}
    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+{\dfrac{1}{x}}\right)}^{x+2}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
             & \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+{\dfrac{1}{x}}\right)}^{x+2}                                                                   \\
             & = \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+{\dfrac{1}{x}}\right)}^{x} \cdot \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+{\dfrac{1}{x}}\right)}^{2} \\
             & = e \cdot 1                                                                                                                     \\
             & = e
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
        \columnbreak{}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1-3x\right)}^{\frac{2}{x}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1-3x\right)}^{\frac{2}{x}} & = \left[\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1-3x\right)}^{-\frac{1}{3x}}\right]^{-6} \\
                                                                      & = e^{6}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
    \end{multicols}

    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+\dfrac{3}{x}\right)}^{\frac{x}{2}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+\dfrac{3}{x}\right)}^{\frac{x}{2}} & = \left[\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+\dfrac{3}{x}\right)}^{\frac{x}{3}}\right]^{\frac{3}{2}} \\
                                                                                & = e^{\frac{3}{2}}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
        \columnbreak{}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(\dfrac{2-3x}{2}\right)}^{\frac{2}{x}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(\dfrac{2-3x}{2}\right)}^{\frac{2}{x}} & = \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1-\dfrac{3x}{2}\right)}^{\frac{2}{x}}                     \\
                                                                                 & = \left[\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1-\dfrac{3x}{2}\right)}^{-\frac{2}{3x}}\right]^{-3} \\
                                                                                 & = e^{-3}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
    \end{multicols}
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Exercise 25.7b}

Find the limit of the following:
\begin{enumerate}
    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+\dfrac{1}{x}\right)}^{\frac{x}{2}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+\dfrac{1}{x}\right)}^{\frac{x}{2}} & = \left[\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+\dfrac{1}{x}\right)}^{x}\right]^{\frac{1}{2}} \\
                                                                                & = e^\frac{1}{2}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
        \columnbreak{}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+\dfrac{3}{x}\right)}^{2x}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+\dfrac{3}{x}\right)}^{2x} & = \left[\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+\dfrac{3}{x}\right)}^{\frac{x}{3}}\right]^{6} \\
                                                                       & = e^{6}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
    \end{multicols}

    \newpage
    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left({\dfrac{x+5}{x}}\right)}^{2x}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left({\dfrac{x+5}{x}}\right)}^{2x} & = \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+\dfrac{5}{x}\right)}^{2x}                            \\
                                                                         & = \left[\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+\dfrac{5}{x}\right)}^{\frac{x}{5}}\right]^{10} \\
                                                                         & = e^{10}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
        \columnbreak{}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+{\dfrac{1}{2x}}\right)}^{-3x}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+{\dfrac{1}{2x}}\right)}^{-3x} & = \left[\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+{\dfrac{1}{2x}}\right)}^{2x}\right]^{-\frac{3}{2}} \\
                                                                           & = e^{-\frac{3}{2}}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
    \end{multicols}
    \vspace{-1cm}
    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left({\dfrac{3-x}{3}}\right)}^{-{\frac{3}{x}}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left({\dfrac{3-x}{3}}\right)}^{-{\frac{3}{x}}} & = \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(1-\dfrac{x}{3}\right)}^{-\frac{3}{x}} \\
                                                                                & = e
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
        \columnbreak{}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+{\dfrac{5}{x}}\right)}^{2-x}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
             & \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+{\dfrac{5}{x}}\right)}^{2-x}                                                                    \\
             & = \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+{\dfrac{5}{x}}\right)}^{-x} \cdot \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+{\dfrac{5}{x}}\right)}^{2} \\
             & = \left[\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+{\dfrac{5}{x}}\right)}^{\frac{x}{5}}\right]^{-5} \cdot 1 = e^{-5}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
    \end{multicols}
    \vspace{-1cm}
    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+\dfrac{3}{2x}\right)}^{3+x}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
             & \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+\dfrac{3}{2x}\right)}^{3+x}                                                                  \\
             & = \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+\dfrac{3}{2x}\right)}^{3} \cdot \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+\dfrac{3}{2x}\right)}^{x} \\
             & = 1 \cdot \left[\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+\dfrac{3}{2x}\right)}^{\frac{2x}{3}}\right]^{\frac{3}{2}}                    \\
             & = e^{\frac{3}{2}}
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(1-4x\right)}^{-\frac{3}{x}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
             & \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(1-4x\right)}^{-\frac{3}{x}}                      \\
             & = \left[\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(1-4x\right)}^{-\frac{1}{4x}}\right]^{12} \\
             & = e^{12}
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}
    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(1+2x\right)}^{1-\frac{2}{x}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
             & \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(1+2x\right)}^{1-\frac{2}{x}}                                                   \\
             & = \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(1+2x\right)}^{1} \cdot \lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(1+2x\right)}^{-\frac{2}{x}} \\
             & = 1 \cdot \left[\lim\limits_{x\to0}{\left(1+2x\right)}^{\frac{1}{2x}}\right]^{-4}                        \\
             & = e^{-4}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
        \columnbreak{}
        \item $\lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left({\dfrac{x+2}{x+1}}\right)}^{x}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left({\dfrac{x+2}{x+1}}\right)}^{x} & = \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+\dfrac{1}{x+1}\right)}^{x}       \\
                                                                          & = \lim\limits_{x\to\infty}{\left(1+\dfrac{1}{x+1}\right)}^{x+1 - 1} \\
                                                                          & = e \div 1                                                          \\
                                                                          & = e
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
    \end{multicols}
\end{enumerate}

\section{Derivatives of Trigonometric Functions}

Here we will derive the derivatives of the sine, cosine, and tangent functions.

Let $y = \sin x$.
\begin{flalign*}
    y + \Delta y                & = \sin(x + \Delta{x})                                                                     \\
    \Delta y                    & = \sin(x + \Delta{x}) - \sin x                                                            \\
                                & = \sin x \cos \Delta{x} + \cos x \sin \Delta{x} - \sin x                                  \\
                                & = \sin x (\cos \Delta{x} - 1) + \cos x \sin \Delta{x}                                     \\
    \dfrac{\Delta y}{\Delta{x}} & = \sin x \dfrac{\cos \Delta{x} - 1}{\Delta{x}} + \cos x \dfrac{\sin \Delta{x}}{\Delta{x}}
\end{flalign*}
\begin{flalign*}
    \because\ \lim\limits_{\Delta{x}\to{0}}{\dfrac{\cos \Delta{x} - 1}{\Delta{x}}} & = \lim\limits_{\Delta{x}\to{0}}{\dfrac{-2 \sin^{2} \dfrac{\Delta{x}}{2}}{\Delta{x}}}                                               \\
                                                                                   & = -\dfrac{1}{2}\lim\limits_{\Delta{x}\to{0}}{\left(\dfrac{\sin \dfrac{\Delta{x}}{2}}{\dfrac{\Delta{x}}{2}}\right) \cdot \Delta{x}} \\
                                                                                   & = 0                                                                                                                                \\
    \lim\limits_{\Delta{x}\to{0}}{\dfrac{\sin \Delta{x}}{\Delta{x}}}               & = 1
\end{flalign*}
\begin{flalign*}
    \therefore\ \dfrac{d}{dx} (\sin x) & = \lim\limits_{\Delta{x}\to{0}}{\dfrac{\Delta y}{\Delta{x}}} \\
                                       & = \sin x \cdot 0 + \cos x \cdot 1                            \\
                                       & = \cos x
\end{flalign*}
\vspace{-1cm}
\begin{mdframed}[style=MyFrame]
    \begin{cequation}
        \dfrac{d}{dx} (\sin{x}) = \cos{x}
    \end{cequation}
\end{mdframed}
\begin{flalign*}
    \because\ \cos x = \sin\left(\dfrac{\pi}{2} - x\right)
\end{flalign*}
\begin{flalign*}
    \therefore\ \dfrac{d}{dx} (\cos x) & = \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\sin\left(\dfrac{\pi}{2} - x\right)\right) \\
                                       & = \cos\left(\dfrac{\pi}{2} - x\right)(-1)                       \\
                                       & = -\sin{x}
\end{flalign*}

\begin{mdframed}[style=MyFrame]
    \begin{cequation}
        \dfrac{d}{dx} (\cos{x}) = -\sin{x}
    \end{cequation}
\end{mdframed}

\begin{flalign*}
    \because\ \tan x = \dfrac{\sin x}{\cos x}
\end{flalign*}
\begin{flalign*}
    \therefore\ \dfrac{d}{dx} (\tan x) & = \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\dfrac{\sin x}{\cos x}\right)                                  \\
                                       & = \dfrac{\cos x \dfrac{d}{dx} (\sin x) - \sin x \dfrac{d}{dx} (\cos x)}{\cos^{2} x} \\
                                       & = \dfrac{\cos x \cos x - \sin x (-\sin x)}{\cos^{2} x}                              \\
                                       & = \dfrac{\cos^{2} x + \sin^{2} x}{\cos^{2} x}                                       \\
                                       & = \dfrac{1}{\cos^{2} x}                                                             \\
                                       & = \sec^{2} x
\end{flalign*}

\begin{mdframed}[style=MyFrame]
    \begin{cequation}
        \dfrac{d}{dx} (\tan{x}) = \sec^{2}{x}
    \end{cequation}
\end{mdframed}

Below are the derivatives of the remaining trigonometric functions.

\begin{mdframed}[style=MyFrame]
    \begin{cequation}
        \dfrac{d}{dx} (\csc{x}) = -\csc{x} \cot{x}
    \end{cequation}
    \begin{cequation}
        \dfrac{d}{dx} (\sec{x}) = \sec{x} \tan{x}
    \end{cequation}
    \begin{cequation}
        \dfrac{d}{dx} (\cot{x}) = -\csc^{2}{x}
    \end{cequation}
\end{mdframed}
For the proofs of these derivatives, see \textit{Thomas' Calculus 14th ed. Exercise 3.5 Question 62}.

\newpage
\subsection{Practice 10}

Find the derivatives of the following functions:
\begin{enumerate}
    \item $y=\cos\left(5x^{2}\right)$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} (\cos{5x^{2}}) & = -\sin{5x^{2}} \cdot 10x \\
                                           & = -10x \sin{5x^{2}}
          \end{flalign*}

    \item $y=\sin^{2}(2x-3)$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} (\sin^{2}(2x-3)) & = 2\sin(2x-3) \cdot \cos(2x-3) \cdot 2 \\
                                             & = 4\sin(2x-3)\cos(2x-3)
          \end{flalign*}
    \item $y=\tan^{4}3x$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} (\tan^{4}3x) & = 4\tan^{3}3x \cdot \sec^{2}3x \cdot 3 \\
                                         & = 12\tan^{3}3x\sec^{2}3x
          \end{flalign*}
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Exercise 25.8}

Find the derivatives of the following functions:
\begin{enumerate}
    \item $y=\sin^{2}x$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} (\sin^{2}x) & = 2\sin x \cdot \cos x \\
                                        & = 2\sin x \cos x       \\
                                        & = \sin 2x
          \end{flalign*}

    \item $y=\sin{3x}-\cos{3x}$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} (\sin{3x}-\cos{3x}) & = 3\cos{3x} + 3\sin{3x}
          \end{flalign*}

          \newpage
    \item $y=\tan4x-\cot5x$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} (\tan4x-\cot5x) & = 4\sec^{2}4x - (-5\csc^{2}5x) \\
                                            & = 4\sec^{2}4x + 5\csc^{2}5x
          \end{flalign*}

    \item $y=\sec3x+\csc5x$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} (\sec3x+\csc5x) & = 3\sec3x\tan3x + (-5\csc5x\cot5x) \\
                                            & = 3\sec3x\tan3x - 5\csc5x\cot5x
          \end{flalign*}

    \item $y=2x\sec x$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} (2x\sec x) & = 2\sec x + 2x\sec x \tan x \\
                                       & = 2\sec x(1+x\tan x)
          \end{flalign*}

    \item $y=\dfrac{2x}{\sin x}$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} \left(\dfrac{2x}{\sin x}\right) & = \dfrac{2\sin x - 2x\cos x}{\sin^{2}x}
          \end{flalign*}

    \item $y=\cos3x^{\circ}$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} (\cos3x^{\circ}) & = -3^\circ\sin3x^{\circ}         \\
                                             & = -\dfrac{\pi}{60}\sin3x^{\circ}
          \end{flalign*}

    \item $y=\cos^{4}(1-2x)$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} (\cos^{4}(1-2x)) & = 4\cos^{3}(1-2x) \cdot (-\sin(1-2x)) \cdot (-2) \\
                                             & = 8\cos^{3}(1-2x)\sin(1-2x)
          \end{flalign*}

          \newpage
    \item $y=\tan^{3}\left(2x^{2}\right)$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} (\tan^{3}(2x^{2})) & = 3\tan^{2}(2x^{2}) \cdot \sec^{2}(2x^{2}) \cdot 4x \\
                                               & = 12x\tan^{2}(2x^{2})\sec^{2}(2x^{2})
          \end{flalign*}

    \item $y=\cos^{2}x-\sin^{2}x$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} (\cos^{2}x-\sin^{2}x) & = 2\cos x \cdot (-\sin x) - 2\sin x \cdot \cos x \\
                                                  & = -2\sin x \cos x - 2\sin x \cos x               \\
                                                  & = -4\sin x \cos x                                \\
                                                  & = -2\sin 2x
          \end{flalign*}

    \item $y=4\sin x\cos x$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} (4\sin x\cos x) & = 4\cos x \cdot \cos x + 4\sin x \cdot (-\sin x) \\
                                            & = 4\cos^{2}x - 4\sin^{2}x                        \\
                                            & = 4(\cos^{2}x - \sin^{2}x)                       \\
                                            & = 4\cos2x
          \end{flalign*}

    \item $y=\sin3x\tan6x$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} (\sin3x\tan6x) & = 3\cos3x \cdot \tan6x + \sin3x \cdot 6\sec^{2}6x \\
                                           & = 3\cos3x\tan6x + 6\sin3x\sec^{2}6x
          \end{flalign*}

    \item $y=\sqrt{\cos2x}$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} (\sqrt{\cos2x}) & = \dfrac{1}{2\sqrt{\cos2x}} \cdot (-\sin2x) \cdot 2 \\
                                            & = -\dfrac{\sin2x}{\sqrt{\cos2x}}
          \end{flalign*}

          \newpage
    \item $y=\sin^{2}\sqrt{1+x^{2}}$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} & = 2\sin\sqrt{1+x^{2}} \cdot \cos\sqrt{1+x^{2}} \cdot \dfrac{1}{2\sqrt{1+x^{2}}} \cdot 2x \\
                            & = \dfrac{2x\sin\sqrt{1+x^{2}}\cos\sqrt{1+x^{2}}}{\sqrt{1+x^{2}}}                         \\
                            & = \dfrac{x\sin2\sqrt{1+x^{2}}}{\sqrt{1+x^{2}}}
          \end{flalign*}

    \item $y=x\tan^{2}(3x-2)$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} \left[x\tan^{2}(3x-2)\right] & = x\cdot 2\tan(3x-2) \cdot \sec^{2}(3x-2) \cdot 3 + \tan^2(3x-2) \\
                                                         & = 6x\tan(3x-2)\sec^{2}(3x-2) + \tan^{2}(3x-2)
          \end{flalign*}

    \item $y=\dfrac{3\sin2x}{\cos x}$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} \left(\dfrac{3\sin2x}{\cos x}\right) & = \dfrac{3 \cdot \cos x \cdot \cos2x\cdot 2 - 3\sin2x\cdot (-\sin x)}{\cos^{2}x} \\
                                                                 & = \dfrac{6\cos2x\cos x + 3\sin2x\sin x}{\cos^{2}x}                               \\
                                                                 & = \dfrac{6\cos2x\cos x + 6\sin x\cos x\sin x}{\cos^{2}x}                         \\
                                                                 & = \dfrac{6\cos x(\cos2x + \sin^{2}x)}{\cos^{2}x}                                 \\
                                                                 & = \dfrac{6(\cos^{2}x - \sin^{2}x + \sin^{2}x)}{\cos x}                           \\
                                                                 & = \dfrac{6\cos^{2}x}{\cos x}                                                     \\
                                                                 & = 6\cos x
          \end{flalign*}

          \newpage
    \item $y={\dfrac{2}{3\tan^{3}x}}$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx} \left({\dfrac{2}{3\tan^{3}x}}\right) & = \dfrac{2}{3}\dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\dfrac{1}{\tan^{3}x}\right) \\
                                                                 & = \dfrac{2}{3}\cdot \dfrac{-3\tan^{2}x\sec^{2}x}{\tan^{6}x}  \\
                                                                 & = \dfrac{-2\sec^{2}x}{\tan^{4}x}                             \\
                                                                 & = \dfrac{-2}{\cos^{2}x\tan^{4}x}                             \\
                                                                 & = \dfrac{-2}{\cos^{2}x\cdot \dfrac{\sin^{4}x}{\cos^{4}x}}    \\
                                                                 & = \dfrac{-2}{\dfrac{\sin^{4}x}{\cos^{2}x}}                   \\
                                                                 & = \dfrac{-2}{\dfrac{\sin^{2}x}{\cos^{2}x}\cdot \sin^{2}x}    \\
                                                                 & = \dfrac{-2}{\tan^{2}x\sin^{2}x}                             \\
                                                                 & = -2\csc^{2}x\cot^{2}x
          \end{flalign*}

    \item $y={\dfrac{1+\cos x}{1-\cos x}}$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\dfrac{1+\cos x}{1-\cos x}\right) & = \dfrac{(1 - \cos x)(-\sin x) - (1 + \cos x)(\sin x)}{{(1 - \cos x)}^{2}}   \\
                                                                   & = \dfrac{-\sin x + \cos x\sin x - \sin x - \cos x\sin x}{{(1 - \cos x)}^{2}} \\
                                                                   & = -\dfrac{2\sin x}{{(1 - \cos x)}^{2}}
          \end{flalign*}

          \newpage
    \item $y={\dfrac{2\tan x}{1-\tan^{2}x}}$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx}\left({\dfrac{2\tan x}{1-\tan^{2}x}}\right) & = \dfrac{2\sec^{2}x(1-\tan^{2}x) - 2\tan x(-2\tan x\sec^{2}x)}{{(1-\tan^{2}x)}^{2}}   \\
                                                                       & = \dfrac{2\sec^{2}x - 2\tan^{2}x\sec^{2}x + 4\tan^{2}x\sec^{2}x}{{(1-\tan^{2}x)}^{2}} \\
                                                                       & = \dfrac{2\sec^{2}x + 2\tan^{2}x\sec^{2}x}{{(1-\tan^{2}x)}^{2}}                       \\
                                                                       & = \dfrac{2\sec^{2}x(1 + \tan^{2}x)}{{(1-\tan^{2}x)}^{2}}                              \\
                                                                       & = \dfrac{2\sec^{2}x\sec^{2}x}{{(1-\tan^{2}x)}^{2}}                                    \\
                                                                       & = \dfrac{2\sec^{4}x}{{(1-\tan^{2}x)}^{2}}                                             \\
                                                                       & = \dfrac{2\sec^{4}x}{{\left(1-\dfrac{\sin^{2}x}{\cos^{2}x}\right)}^{2}}               \\
                                                                       & = \dfrac{2\sec^{4}x}{{\left(\dfrac{\cos^{2}x - \sin^{2}x}{\cos^{2}x}\right)}^{2}}     \\
                                                                       & = \dfrac{2\sec^{4}x}{{\left(\dfrac{\cos2x}{\cos^{2}x}\right)}^{2}}                    \\
                                                                       & = \dfrac{2\sec^{4}x}{\dfrac{\sec^{4}x}{\sec^{2}2x}}                                   \\
                                                                       & = 2\sec^{4}x \cdot \dfrac{\sec^{2}2x}{\sec^{4}x}                                      \\
                                                                       & = 2\sec^{2}2x
          \end{flalign*}

          \newpage
    \item $y={\dfrac{\sin\left(2x-{\dfrac{\pi}{4}}\right)}{\sin\left(2x+{\dfrac{\pi}{4}}\right)}}$
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx}\left({\dfrac{\sin\left(2x-{\dfrac{\pi}{4}}\right)}{\sin\left(2x+{\dfrac{\pi}{4}}\right)}}\right) & = \dfrac{2\cos\left(2x-{\dfrac{\pi}{4}}\right)\cdot \sin\left(2x+{\dfrac{\pi}{4}}\right) - 2\sin\left(2x-{\dfrac{\pi}{4}}\right)\cdot \cos\left(2x+{\dfrac{\pi}{4}}\right)}{{\sin^{2}\left(2x+{\dfrac{\pi}{4}}\right)}} \\
                                                                                                                             & = \dfrac{\sin x + \sin \dfrac{\pi}{2} - \sin x + \sin \dfrac{\pi}{2}}{{\sin^{2}\left(2x+{\dfrac{\pi}{4}}\right)}}                                                                                                       \\
                                                                                                                             & = \dfrac{2\sin \dfrac{\pi}{2}}{{\sin^{2}\left(2x+{\dfrac{\pi}{4}}\right)}}                                                                                                                                              \\
                                                                                                                             & = \dfrac{2}{{\sin^{2}\left(2x+{\dfrac{\pi}{4}}\right)}}                                                                                                                                                                 \\
                                                                                                                             & = 2\csc^{2}\left(2x+{\dfrac{\pi}{4}}\right)                                                                                                                                                                             \\
          \end{flalign*}
\end{enumerate}

\begin{enumerate}
    \setcounter{enumi}{20}
    \item Given the function $y = \dfrac{x}{2 + \cos x}$. Find the derivative value when
          $x = 0$, $x = \dfrac{\pi}{2}$, and $x = \pi$. \sol{} \vspace{-1cm}
          \begin{multicols}{2}
              \begin{flalign*}
                  y'    & = \dfrac{(2 + \cos x)(1) - (x)(-\sin x)}{{(2 + \cos x)}^{2}} \\
                        & = \dfrac{2 + \cos x + x\sin x}{{(2 + \cos x)}^{2}}           \\
                  \\
                  y'(0) & = \dfrac{2 + \cos 0 + 0\sin 0}{{(2 + \cos 0)}^{2}}           \\
                        & = \dfrac{2 + 1}{{{(2 + 1)}}^{2}}                             \\
                        & = \dfrac{1}{3}
              \end{flalign*}
              \vfill{}\null{}
              \columnbreak{}
              \begin{flalign*}
                  y'\left(\dfrac{\pi}{2}\right) & = \dfrac{2 + \cos \dfrac{\pi}{2} + \dfrac{\pi}{2}\sin \dfrac{\pi}{2}}{{\left(2 + \cos \dfrac{\pi}{2}\right)}^{2}} \\
                                                & = \dfrac{2 + 0 + \dfrac{\pi}{2}(1)}{{(2 + 0)}^{2}}                                                                \\
                                                & = \dfrac{2 + \dfrac{\pi}{2}}{4}                                                                                   \\
                                                & = \dfrac{1}{2} + \dfrac{\pi}{8}                                                                                   \\
                  \\
                  y'(\pi)                       & = \dfrac{2 + \cos \pi + \pi\sin \pi}{{(2 + \cos \pi)}^{2}}                                                        \\
                                                & = \dfrac{2 - 1 + \pi(0)}{{(2 - 1)}^{2}}                                                                           \\
                                                & = \dfrac{1}{1}                                                                                                    \\
                                                & = 1
              \end{flalign*}
          \end{multicols}

    \item If the function $y = \sec x + \tan x$, prove that $\dfrac{dy}{dx} = y\sec x$.
          \prooff{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              y              & = \sec x + \tan x           \\
              \dfrac{dy}{dx} & = \sec x \tan x + \sec^{2}x \\
                             & = \sec x(\tan x + \sec x)   \\
                             & = y\sec x \qed
          \end{flalign*}

    \item If the function $y = \sqrt{\dfrac{1 - \cos x}{1 + \cos x}}$, find
          $\dfrac{dy}{dx}$. \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{dy}{dx} & = \dfrac{1}{2}\left(\dfrac{1 - \cos x}{1 + \cos x}\right)^{-\frac{1}{2}} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\dfrac{1 - \cos x}{1 + \cos x}\right)                \\
                             & = \dfrac{1}{2}\left(\dfrac{1 + \cos x}{1 - \cos x}\right)^{\frac{1}{2}} \cdot \dfrac{(1 + \cos x)(\sin x) - (1 - \cos x)(-\sin x)}{{(1 + \cos x)}^{2}} \\
                             & = \dfrac{1}{2}\left(\dfrac{1 + \cos x}{1 - \cos x}\right)^{\frac{1}{2}} \cdot \dfrac{\sin x(1 + \cos x + 1 - \cos x)}{{(1 + \cos x)}^{2}}              \\
                             & = \dfrac{1}{2}\dfrac{\sqrt{1 + \cos x}}{\sqrt{1 - \cos x}} \cdot \dfrac{2\sin x}{{(1 + \cos x)}^{2}}                                                   \\
                             & = \dfrac{\sin x\sqrt{1 + \cos x}}{{(1 + \cos x)}^{2}\sqrt{1 - \cos x}}                                                                                 \\
                             & = \dfrac{\sin x}{{(1 + \cos x)}^{\frac{3}{2}}\sqrt{1 - \cos x}}
          \end{flalign*}

    \item If the function $r = \sin 3t - 2\cos t$, find $\dfrac{d^2r}{dt^2}$ when $t =
              \dfrac{\pi}{3}$. \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{dr}{dt}     & = 3\cos 3t + 2\sin t  \\
              \dfrac{d^2r}{dt^2} & = -9\sin 3t + 2\cos t
          \end{flalign*}
          When $t = \dfrac{\pi}{3}$,
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d^2r}{dt^2} & = -9\sin \pi + 2\cos \dfrac{\pi}{3} \\
                                 & = 0 + 2\left(\dfrac{1}{2}\right)    \\
                                 & = 1
          \end{flalign*}
\end{enumerate}

\newpage

\subsection{Thomas' Calculus 14th ed. Exercise 3.5}

\begin{enumerate}
    \setcounter{enumi}{61}
    \item Derive the formula for the derivative with respect to $x$ of
          \begin{multicols}{3}
              \begin{enumerate}[label=(\alph*)]
                  \item $\sec x$
                  \item $\csc x$
                  \item $\cot x$
              \end{enumerate}
          \end{multicols}
          \sol{}
          \begin{flalign*}
              \dfrac{d}{dx}(\sec x) & = \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\dfrac{1}{\cos x}\right)         \\
                                    & = -\dfrac{1}{\cos^{2}x}\cdot (-\sin x)                \\
                                    & = \dfrac{\sin x}{\cos^{2}x}                           \\
                                    & = \dfrac{1}{\cos x} \cdot \dfrac{\sin x}{\cos x}      \\
                                    & = \sec x \tan x                                       \\
              \\
              \dfrac{d}{dx}(\csc x) & = \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\dfrac{1}{\sin x}\right)         \\
                                    & = -\dfrac{1}{\sin^{2}x}\cdot \cos x                   \\
                                    & = -\dfrac{\cos x}{\sin^{2}x}                          \\
                                    & = -\dfrac{1}{\sin x} \cdot \dfrac{\cos x}{\sin x}     \\
                                    & = -\csc x \cot x                                      \\
              \\
              \dfrac{d}{dx}(\cot x) & = \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\dfrac{\cos x}{\sin x}\right)    \\
                                    & = \dfrac{\sin x(-\sin x) - \cos x(\cos x)}{\sin^{2}x} \\
                                    & = \dfrac{-\sin^{2}x - \cos^{2}x}{\sin^{2}x}           \\
                                    & = -\dfrac{1}{\sin^{2}x}                               \\
                                    & = -\csc^{2}x
          \end{flalign*}
\end{enumerate}

\section{Derivatives of Exponential Functions}

\subsection*{Derivative of Natural Logarithmic Functions}

Let $y = \ln x$ where $x > 0$.
\begin{flalign*}
    y + \Delta y                & = \ln (x + \Delta{x})                                                                                              \\
    \Delta y                    & = \ln (x + \Delta{x}) - \ln x                                                                                      \\
                                & = \ln \left(\frac{x + \Delta{x}}{x}\right)                                                                         \\
                                & = \ln \left(1 + \dfrac{\Delta{x}}{x}\right)                                                                        \\
    \dfrac{\Delta y}{\Delta{x}} & = \dfrac{1}{\Delta{x}}\ln \left(1 + \dfrac{\Delta{x}}{x}\right)                                                    \\
                                & = \dfrac{1}{\Delta{x}}\cdot \dfrac{x}{\Delta{x}} \cdot \ln \left(1 + \dfrac{\Delta{x}}{x}\right)                   \\
                                & = \dfrac{1}{x}\ln {\left(1 + \dfrac{\Delta{x}}{x}\right)}^{\frac{x}{\Delta{x}}}                                    \\
    \dfrac{dy}{dx}              & = \lim_{\Delta{x}\to{0}} \dfrac{\Delta y}{\Delta{x}}                                                               \\
                                & = \dfrac{1}{x}\lim_{\Delta{x}\to{0}} \ln {\left(1 + \dfrac{\Delta{x}}{x}\right)}^{\frac{x}{\Delta{x}}}             \\
                                & = \dfrac{1}{x}\ln\left(\lim_{\Delta{x}\to{0}} {\left(1 + \dfrac{\Delta{x}}{x}\right)}^{\frac{x}{\Delta{x}}}\right) \\
                                & = \dfrac{1}{x}\ln e                                                                                                \\
                                & = \dfrac{1}{x}
\end{flalign*}

\begin{mdframed}[style=MyFrame]
    \begin{cequation}
        \dfrac{d}{dx} (\ln{x}) = \dfrac{1}{x}
    \end{cequation}
\end{mdframed}

If $x < 0$, then $-x > 0$.
\begin{flalign*}
    \dfrac{d}{dx} (\ln -x) & = \dfrac{1}{-x}\dfrac{d}{dx} (-x) \\
                           & = \dfrac{1}{x}
\end{flalign*}

\begin{mdframed}[style=MyFrame]
    \begin{cequation}
        \dfrac{d}{dx} (\ln\vert{x}\vert) = \dfrac{1}{x}
    \end{cequation}
\end{mdframed}

\subsection*{Derivative of Other Logarithmic Functions}

\begin{flalign*}
    \text{Let } y  & = \log_{a}x                                       \\
                   & = \dfrac{\ln x}{\ln a}                            \\
                   & = \dfrac{1}{\ln a}\ln x                           \\
    \dfrac{dy}{dx} & = \dfrac{1}{\ln a}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx} (\ln x)     \\
                   & = \dfrac{1}{\ln a}\cdot \left(\dfrac{1}{x}\right) \\
                   & = \dfrac{1}{x\ln a}
\end{flalign*}

\begin{mdframed}[style=MyFrame]
    \begin{cequation}
        \dfrac{d}{dx} (\log_{a}x) = \dfrac{1}{x\ln{a}}
    \end{cequation}
\end{mdframed}

Generally, when solving for the derivative of a logarithmic function, we can
first convert it to a natural logarithmic function and then solve for the
derivative.

\subsection{Practice 11}

Find the derivative of the following functions:
\begin{enumerate}
    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=\ln\left(x^{2}-2x+1\right)$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\dfrac{1}{x^{2}-2x+1}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(x^{2}-2x+1\right) \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{{(x - 1)}^2}\cdot \left(2x-2\right)                   \\
               & =\dfrac{2(x-1)}{{(x - 1)}^2}                                     \\
               & =\dfrac{2}{x-1}
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $y=\log_{2}\sin3x$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\dfrac{1}{\sin3x\ln2}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\sin3x\right) \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{\sin3x\ln2}\cdot 3\cos3x                          \\
               & =\dfrac{3\cos3x}{\sin3x\ln2}
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}

    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=\ln(\sec x)$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\dfrac{1}{\sec x}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\sec x\right) \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{\sec x}\cdot \sec x\tan x                     \\
               & =\tan x
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $y=x\ln x$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\ln x+\dfrac{x}{x} \\
               & =\ln x+1
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}

    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=\ln{\dfrac{1+x}{1-x}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\dfrac{1}{\dfrac{1+x}{1-x}}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\dfrac{1+x}{1-x}\right) \\
               & =\dfrac{1-x}{1+x}\cdot \dfrac{1-x+1+x}{(1-x)^{2}}                            \\
               & =\dfrac{1-x}{1+x}\cdot \dfrac{2}{(1-x)^{2}}                                  \\
               & =\dfrac{2(1-x)}{(1+x)(1-x)^{2}}                                              \\
               & =\dfrac{2}{(1+x)(1-x)}                                                       \\
               & =\dfrac{2}{1-x^{2}}
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $y=\log_{2}{\sqrt{1+x^{2}}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\dfrac{1}{\sqrt{1+x^{2}}\ln2}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\sqrt{1+x^{2}}\right) \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{\sqrt{1+x^{2}}\ln2}\cdot \dfrac{1}{2\sqrt{1+x^{2}}}\cdot 2x       \\
               & =\dfrac{x}{(1+x^{2})\ln2}
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}
\end{enumerate}

\subsection{Exercise 25.9}

Find the derivative of the following functions:
\begin{enumerate}
    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=\ln\left(5x-3\right)$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\dfrac{1}{5x-3}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(5x-3\right) \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{5x-3}\cdot 5                              \\
               & =\dfrac{5}{5x-3}
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $y=\ln\left(a x^{3}\right)$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\dfrac{1}{ax^{3}}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(ax^{3}\right) \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{ax^{3}}\cdot 3ax^2                            \\
               & =\dfrac{3}{x}
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}

    \newpage
    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=\ln{\dfrac{3}{x^{2}}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\dfrac{1}{\dfrac{3}{x^{2}}}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\dfrac{3}{x^{2}}\right) \\
               & =\dfrac{x^2}{3}\cdot \dfrac{-6}{x^{3}}                                       \\
               & =-\dfrac{2}{x}
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $y=\ln\left(2x^{2}-3x+4\right)$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\dfrac{1}{2x^{2}-3x+4}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(2x^{2}-3x+4\right) \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{2x^{2}-3x+4}\cdot \left(4x-3\right)                     \\
               & =\dfrac{4x-3}{2x^{2}-3x+4}
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}

    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=\log_{5}(3x)$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\dfrac{1}{3x\ln5}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(3x\right) \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{3x\ln5}\cdot 3                            \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{x\ln5}
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $y=\log_{2}\left(x^{2}-4x\!+\!3\right)$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\dfrac{1}{(x^{2}-4x+3)\ln2}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(x^{2}-4x+3\right) \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{(x^{2}-4x+3)\ln2}\cdot (2x-4)                               \\
               & =\dfrac{2x-4}{(x^{2}-4x+3)\ln2}
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}

    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=\log_{a}\left(2a x^{2}-4a x\right)$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\dfrac{1}{(2ax^{2}-4ax)\ln a}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(2ax^{2}-4ax\right) & \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{2a(x^{2}-2x)\ln a}\cdot (4ax-4a)                                 \\
               & =\dfrac{4a(x-1)}{2a(x^{2}-2x)\ln a}                                         \\
               & =\dfrac{2(x-1)}{(x^{2}-2x)\ln a}
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $y=\log_{a}\left(\ln x\right)$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\dfrac{1}{\ln x\ln a}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\ln x\right) \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{\ln x\ln a}\cdot \dfrac{1}{x}                    \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{(x\ln x)\ln a}
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}

    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=3x^{2}\ln\left(5x\right)$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =3x^{2}\cdot \dfrac{1}{5x}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(5x\right)+\ln(5x)\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(3x^{2}\right) & \\
               & =\dfrac{3x}{5} \cdot 5+\ln(5x)\cdot 6x                                                                       \\
               & =3x+6x\ln5x
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
        \item $y=\ln\left(\cos^{2}x\right)$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\dfrac{1}{\cos^{2}x}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\cos^{2}x\right)           \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{\cos^{2}x}\cdot 2\cos x\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\cos x\right) \\
               & =\dfrac{2\cos x}{\cos^{2}x}\cdot (-\sin x)                               \\
               & =-\dfrac{2\sin x}{\cos x}                                                \\
               & =-2\tan x
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
    \end{multicols}

    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=\ln{(4x+3)}^{2}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\dfrac{1}{(4x+3)^{2}}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left[(4x+3)^{2}\right] \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{(4x+3)^{2}}\cdot 2(4x+3)\cdot 4                       \\
               & =\dfrac{8}{4x+3}
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $y=\log_{5}\left(2x^{2}-3\right)$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\dfrac{1}{(2x^{2}-3)\ln5}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(2x^{2}-3\right) \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{(2x^{2}-3)\ln5}\cdot 4x                                 \\
               & =\dfrac{4x}{(2x^{2}-3)\ln5}
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}

    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=\log_{8}{\sqrt{x^{2}-2}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\dfrac{1}{\sqrt{x^{2}-2}\ln8}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\sqrt{x^{2}-2}\right)                            \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{\sqrt{x^{2}-2}\ln8}\cdot \dfrac{1}{2\sqrt{x^{2}-2}}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(x^{2}-2\right) & \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{2(x^{2}-2)\ln8}\cdot 2x                                                                      \\
               & =\dfrac{x}{(x^{2}-2)\ln8}
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $y=\log_{b}(\sin5x)$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\dfrac{1}{\sin5x\ln b}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\sin5x\right) \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{\sin5x\ln b}\cdot 5\cos5x                          \\
               & =\dfrac{5\cos5x}{\sin5x\ln b}                                 \\
               & = \dfrac{5\cot5x}{\ln b}
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}

    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=\log{(5x)}+\ln{(\tan{x})}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\dfrac{1}{5x\ln10} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(5x) + \dfrac{1}{\tan x} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(\tan x) & \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{5x\ln10} \cdot 5 + \dfrac{1}{\tan x} \cdot \sec^{2}x                               \\
               & =\dfrac{1}{x\ln10} + \dfrac{\sec^{2}x}{\tan x}
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $y=\ln^{2}(\sec x)$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = 2\ln(\sec x) \cdot \dfrac{1}{\sec x} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(\sec x) \\
               & = 2\ln(\sec x) \cdot \dfrac{1}{\sec x} \cdot \sec x \tan x         \\
               & = 2\ln(\sec x) \cdot \tan x                                        \\
               & = 2\tan x \ln(\sec x)
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}

    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=\log_{3}{\dfrac{2}{x^{2}-1}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = \dfrac{1}{\left(\dfrac{2}{x^{2}-1}\right)\ln3} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\dfrac{2}{x^{2}-1}\right) \\
               & = \dfrac{x^{2}-1}{2\ln3} \cdot \dfrac{-4x}{(x^{2}-1)^{2}}                                           \\
               & = -\dfrac{2x}{(x^{2}-1)\ln3}
        \end{flalign*}
        \item $y={\dfrac{1+\ln x}{1-\ln x}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = \dfrac{(1-\ln x)\cdot \dfrac{1}{x} + (1+\ln x)\cdot \dfrac{1}{x}}{(1-\ln x)^{2}} \\
               & = \dfrac{1-\ln x + 1 + \ln x}{x(1-\ln x)^{2}}                                      \\
               & = \dfrac{2}{x(1-\ln x)^{2}}
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}

    \newpage
    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=\ln{\dfrac{2+x^{2}}{2-x^{2}}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = \dfrac{1}{\dfrac{2+x^{2}}{2-x^{2}}}\cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\dfrac{2+x^{2}}{2-x^{2}}\right)   \\
               & = \dfrac{1}{2+x^{2}} \cdot \dfrac{2x(2-x^{2}) + 2x(2+x^{2})}{2-x^{2}}                           \\
               & = \dfrac{1}{2+x^{2}} \cdot \dfrac{2x(2 - x^2 + 2 + x^2)}{2-x^{2}}                             & \\
               & = \dfrac{1}{2+x^{2}} \cdot \dfrac{8x}{2-x^{2}}                                                  \\
               & = \dfrac{8x}{(2+x^{2})(2-x^{2})}                                                                \\
               & = \dfrac{8x}{4-x^{4}}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
        \item $y=\ln{\dfrac{2\sin x}{\sec x}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = \dfrac{1}{\dfrac{2\sin x}{\sec x}} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(\dfrac{2\sin x}{\sec x}\right)          & \\
               & = \dfrac{\sec x}{2\sin x} \cdot \dfrac{2\cos x \cdot \sec x - 2\sin x \cdot \sec x \tan x}{\sec^{2}x}   \\
               & = \dfrac{\sec x}{2\sin x} \cdot \dfrac{2\sec x(\cos x - \sin x \tan x)}{\sec^{2}x}                      \\
               & = \dfrac{\sec^2 x\left(\cos x - \sin x \tan x\right)}{\sin x\sec^{2}x}                                  \\
               & = \dfrac{\cos x - \sin x \tan x}{\sin x}                                                                \\
               & = \dfrac{\cos x}{\sin x} - \dfrac{\sin x \tan x}{\sin x}                                                \\
               & = \cot x - \tan x
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
    \end{multicols}
\end{enumerate}

\newpage
\section{Derivatives of Logarithmic Functions}

\subsection*{Derivative of exponential functions $y = e^{x}$}

If $y = e^{x}$, then $\ln y = e^{x} = x$.
\begin{flalign*}
    \text{Differentiate both sides with respect to $x$, we get } \dfrac{1}{y}\cdot\dfrac{dy}{dx} & = 1     & \\
    \dfrac{dy}{dx}                                                                               & = y       \\
                                                                                                 & = e^{x}
\end{flalign*}

\begin{mdframed}[style=MyFrame]
    \begin{cequation}
        \dfrac{d}{dx} (e^{x}) = e^{x}
    \end{cequation}
\end{mdframed}

\subsection*{Derivative of other exponential functions}

Let $y = a^{x}$ where $a > 0$.
\begin{flalign*}
    \text{Take the natural logarithm of both sides, we get } \ln y                               & = \ln a^{x}  & \\
                                                                                                 & = x\ln a       \\
    \\
    \text{Differentiate both sides with respect to $x$, we get } \dfrac{1}{y}\cdot\dfrac{dy}{dx} & = \ln a        \\
    \dfrac{dy}{dx}                                                                               & = y\ln a       \\
                                                                                                 & = a^{x}\ln a
\end{flalign*}

Generally, when solving for the derivative of an exponential function, we can
first convert it to a natural exponential function and then solve for the
derivative.

\newpage
\subsection{Practice 12}

Find the derivative of the following functions:
\begin{enumerate}
    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=e^{-3x}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = e^{-3x} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(-3x) \\
               & = e^{-3x} \cdot (-3)               \\
               & = -3e^{-3x}
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $y=-e^{-{\frac{1}{3}x}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = -e^{-{\frac{1}{3}x}} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(-{\frac{1}{3}x}\right) \\
               & = -e^{-{\frac{1}{3}x}} \cdot \left(-{\frac{1}{3}}\right)               \\
               & = \dfrac{1}{3}e^{-{\frac{x}{3}}}
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}

    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=2a^{5x}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = 2a^{5x}\ln a \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(5x) \\
               & = 2a^{5x}\ln a \cdot 5                 \\
               & = 10a^{5x}\ln a
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $y=a^{2x}-e^{-x}+x^{a}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = a^{2x}\ln a \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(2x) - e^{-x} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(-x) + ax^{a-1} & \\
               & = a^{2x}\ln a \cdot 2 + e^{-x} + ax^{a-1}                                           \\
               & = 2a^{2x}\ln a + e^{-x} + ax^{a-1}
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}

    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y={\left(e^{x}+{\dfrac{1}{e^{x}}}\right)}^{2}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = 2\left(e^{x}+{\dfrac{1}{e^{x}}}\right) \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(e^{x}+{\dfrac{1}{e^{x}}}\right) \\
               & = 2\left(e^{x}+{\dfrac{1}{e^{x}}}\right) \cdot \left(e^{x}-{\dfrac{1}{e^{x}}}\right)              \\
               & = 2\left(e^{2x}-{\dfrac{1}{e^{2x}}}\right)                                                        \\
               & = 2e^{2x}-2e^{-2x}
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $y={\dfrac{e^{3x}-e^{-3x}}{e^{x}}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & =\left(e^{2x} - e^{-4x}\right)'                                     \\
               & = e^{2x} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(2x) - e^{-4x} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(-4x) \\
               & = 2e^{2x} + 4e^{-4x}
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}
\end{enumerate}

\newpage
\subsection{Exercise 25.10}

Find the derivative of the following functions:
\begin{enumerate}
    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=e^{-5x}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = e^{-5x} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(-5x) \\
               & = e^{-5x} \cdot (-5)               \\
               & = -5e^{-5x}
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $y=3e^{-{\frac{1}{3}}x}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = 3e^{-{\frac{1}{3}}x} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}\left(-{\frac{1}{3}}x\right) \\
               & = 3e^{-{\frac{1}{3}}x} \cdot \left(-{\frac{1}{3}}\right)               \\
               & = -e^{-{\frac{x}{3}}}
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}

    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=e^{x^{2}+3x-1}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = e^{x^{2}+3x-1} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(x^{2}+3x-1) \\
               & = e^{x^{2}+3x-1} \cdot (2x+3)                    \\
               & = (2x+3)e^{x^{2}+3x-1}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
        \item $y=e^{5x}\cdot e^{-6x}\cdot4e^{2}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = (4e^{-x + 2})'                          \\
               & = 4e^{-x + 2} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(-x + 2) \\
               & = 4e^{-x + 2} \cdot (-1)                  \\
               & = -4e^{2 - x}
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
    \end{multicols}

    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=5^{2x}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = 5^{2x}\ln 5 \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(2x) \\
               & = 5^{2x}\ln 5 \cdot 2                 \\
               & = 2(5^{2x})\ln 5
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $y={(3b)}^{7x}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = (3b)^{7x}\ln(3b) \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(7x) \\
               & = (3b)^{7x}\ln(3b) \cdot 7                 \\
               & = 7(3b)^{7x}\ln(3b)
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}

    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=4^{3-2x^2}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = 4^{3-2x^2}\ln 4 \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(3-2x^2) \\
               & = 4^{3-2x^2}\ln 4 \cdot (-4x)                 \\
               & = -4(4^{3-2x^2})x\ln 4
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $y=4^{2x}-4^{-2x}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = 4^{2x}\ln 4 \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(2x) - 4^{-2x}\ln 4 \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(-2x) \\
               & = 4^{2x}\ln 4 \cdot 2 - 4^{-2x}\ln 4 \cdot (-2)                               \\
               & = 2(4^{2x} + 4^{-2x})\ln 4
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}

    \newpage
    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=3e^{\tan x}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = 3e^{\tan x} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(\tan x) \\
               & = 3e^{\tan x} \cdot \sec^{2}x             \\
               & = 3e^{\tan x}\sec^{2}x
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $y=e^{x}\ln x$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = e^x \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(\ln x) + \ln x \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(e^x) \\
               & = e^x \cdot \dfrac{1}{x} + e^x \cdot \ln x                        \\
               & = \dfrac{e^x}{x} + e^x \ln x
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}

    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y=3^{2x}\cos5x$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = \cos 5x \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(3^{2x}) + 3^{2x} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(\cos 5x) & \\
               & = \cos 5x 3^{2x}\ln 3 \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(2x)                                 \\
               & \ \ \ \ - 3^{2x}\sin 5x \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(5x)                               \\
               & = 3^{2x}(2\ln 3)\cos 5x - 5\cdot 3^{2x}\sin 5x
        \end{flalign*}
        \vfill{}\null{}
        \item $y={\dfrac{e^{x}+1}{e^{x}-1}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = \dfrac{(e^x - 1) \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(e^x + 1) - (e^x + 1) \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(e^x - 1)}{(e^x - 1)^2} & \\
               & = \dfrac{(e^x - 1) \cdot e^x - (e^x + 1) \cdot e^x}{(e^x - 1)^2}                                         \\
               & = \dfrac{e^x(e^x - 1 - e^x - 1)}{(e^x - 1)^2}                                                            \\
               & = -\dfrac{2e^{2x}}{(e^x - 1)^2}
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}

    \begin{multicols}{2}
        \item $y={\dfrac{e^{2x}-e^{-2x}}{2e^{x}}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = \left(\dfrac{1}{2}e^{x} - \dfrac{1}{2}e^{-3x}\right)'                                 \\
               & = \dfrac{1}{2}e^x \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(x) - \dfrac{1}{2}e^{-3x} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(-3x) \\
               & = \dfrac{1}{2}e^x \cdot 1 - \dfrac{3}{2}e^{-3x} \cdot (-3)                              \\
               & = \dfrac{1}{2}e^{x} + \dfrac{3}{2}e^{-3x}
        \end{flalign*}

        \item $y={\dfrac{3e^{5x}-2e^{-2x}}{6e^{x}}}$
        \sol{}
        \begin{flalign*}
            y' & = \left(\dfrac{1}{2}e^{4x} - \dfrac{1}{3}e^{-3x}\right)'                                    \\
               & = \dfrac{1}{2}e^{4x} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(4x) - \dfrac{1}{3}e^{-3x} \cdot \dfrac{d}{dx}(-3x) \\
               & = \dfrac{1}{2}e^{4x} \cdot 4 - \dfrac{1}{3}e^{-3x} \cdot (-3)                               \\
               & = 2e^{4x} + e^{-3x}
        \end{flalign*}
    \end{multicols}
\end{enumerate}
